#Title: An Off-line Scan of the BATSE Daily Records and a Large Uniform Sample 
#       of Gamma-Ray Bursts
#Authors: Stern B.E.,  Tikhomirova Y., Kompaneets D., Svensson R., Poutanen J.  
#Table: GRB characteristics
#================================================================================
#Byte-by-byte Description of file: datafile2.txt
#--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#   Bytes Format Units            Label     Explanations
#--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#   1-  5 I5     d                TJD       Event identifier
#       6 A1     ---              Char      Character of the event identifier   
#   8- 12 I5     s                Start     Start of the event within the day (1)     
#  14- 17 I4     ---              Trigger   BATSE trigger number, or 1 for 
#                                            non-triggered events
#  19- 24 F6.3   "photons/cm2/s"  Flux      Peak flux in the 50 - 300 keV range 
#  26- 30 F5.1   deg              RAdeg     Right Ascension (J2000) 
#  32- 36 F5.1   deg              DEdeg     Declination (J2000)
#  38- 41 F4.1   deg              Error     Size of the 1 sigma confidence area
#  43- 45 I3     s                T90       Duration rounded to integer seconds (2)
#  47- 49 I3     ---              N50       Number of 1.024 s bins  where the signal 
#                                            exceeds 50% of the peak value (2)
#      51 I1     ---              K98       Identification with the K98 catalog (3)
#      53 I1     ---              Gap       Flag characterizing the data quality (4)
#--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#Note (1): The start time is defined as the beginning of the first 1.024 s bin
#          within the burst window where the fitted background was exceeded by 4
#          sigma in the  50-300 keV range.  If there was no 4 sigma excess in
#          1.024 s bins, the procedure is repeated with 2.048 s, 4.096 s, 8.192 s
#          bins.  If the burst consists of a few widely spaced episodes, the GRB
#          window covers the highest peak and does not necessarily coincide with
#          the actual beginning.
#Note (2): The value of T90 for weak short events is strongly affected by the
#          Poisson noise and should be used with care.  Poisson fluctuations
#          cause an overestimation of T90 for such events.  If N50 is 1, the peak
#          flux is  below 0.5 photons/cm2/s and T90 is within 4 s, then this is
#          probably a one-bin event with T90<1 s.  Therefore we do not recommend
#          to use this duration distribution for a statistical analysis for
#          bursts of durations less than a few seconds.
#Note (3): Flag equal to 1 means that the event exist in the K98 catalog.  The
#          agreement in the GRB location sometimes is very poor (difference up to
#          45 deg).  We consider bursts to coincide if they overlap in time.  If
#          they  differ in time by 100-300 s but have close locations, we
#          considered them identical anyway.
#Note (4):
#    0 = normal data;
#    1 = estimate of duration is problematic because of a data gap;
#    2 = estimate of the peak flux is problematic because of a data gap;
#    3 = 1 and 2 simultaneously.
#--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
